        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2871272596" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4790825707798364362">This is a timely and powerful portrayal of the plight of the migrant. An innocent mother and her young son desperately and illegally attempt to enter the US from Mexico while fleeing from a cartel. The beginning is brutal and the tension never ceases. The cartel’s savagery is not the focus of the novel but it is the impetus. At its heart, this is a novel about victims and there are victims aplenty. No one is to be trusted. Although, amid much cold-blooded barbarity and those out to make quick bu</span>
  <span id="freeText4790825707798364362" style="display:none">This is a timely and powerful portrayal of the plight of the migrant. An innocent mother and her young son desperately and illegally attempt to enter the US from Mexico while fleeing from a cartel. The beginning is brutal and the tension never ceases. The cartel’s savagery is not the focus of the novel but it is the impetus. At its heart, this is a novel about victims and there are victims aplenty. No one is to be trusted. Although, amid much cold-blooded barbarity and those out to make quick buck at the expense of the downtrodden, there are good souls who provide food, water, and shelter to the migrants. Be prepared to read this with your heart in your throat. I know of a certain occupant of the White House who would benefit greatly from reading this book but, alas, he does not read. Let’s hope American Dirt opens the eyes of others. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4790825707798364362" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3033468809" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3033468809" />
    <a title="Lindsay - Traveling Sisters Book Reviews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/54886546-lindsay---traveling-sisters-book-reviews"><img alt="Lindsay - Traveling Sisters Book Reviews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1472552597p2/54886546.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3033468809?book_show_action=true">Feb 24, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lindsay - Traveling Sisters Book Reviews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lindsay - Traveling Sisters Book Reviews" href="/user/show/54886546-lindsay---traveling-sisters-book-reviews">Lindsay - Traveling Sisters Book Reviews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54886546-lindsay---traveling-sisters-book-reviews?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54886546-lindsay---traveling-sisters-book-reviews?shelf=2020-favourites">2020-favourites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3033468809" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1677472311345224953">5+ outstanding stars! <br/><br/>I was invested in this story from page one! This novel starts with a gut wrenching, pulse pounding, horrific opening scene. One that I’ll never forget reading. We are introduced to our main characters, eight-year-old Luca and his mother Lydia. Luca and Lydia are forced to flee their hometown city of Acapulco, on the run from a powerful cartel. Their goal is to reach “el norte” where they hope to find freedom and safety.<br/><br/>The writing was exquisite and atmospheric - I was hangi</span>
  <span id="freeText1677472311345224953" style="display:none">5+ outstanding stars! <br /><br />I was invested in this story from page one! This novel starts with a gut wrenching, pulse pounding, horrific opening scene. One that I’ll never forget reading. We are introduced to our main characters, eight-year-old Luca and his mother Lydia. Luca and Lydia are forced to flee their hometown city of Acapulco, on the run from a powerful cartel. Their goal is to reach “el norte” where they hope to find freedom and safety.<br /><br />The writing was exquisite and atmospheric - I was hanging on every word. The pace was perfect and kept me on the edge of my seat in anticipation of what would come next. The flow was smooth, moving through Luca and Lydia’s struggles while maintaining hope of reaching a better place. I enjoyed meeting the many characters that Luca and Lydia encountered along their travels, each one adding a deeper layer to their personal journey. The storyline itself is one that I found fascinating - a unique plot that I learned a lot from. This is a book I was thinking deeply about even when I wasn’t reading it. These characters and their journey will stay on my mind for a long time. A fantastic novel that I highly recommend!<br /><br />Please note: I haven’t looked into the controversy surrounding this book. I’ve read some reviews but haven’t researched what all the controversial buzz is about. I wanted to read this with an unbiased mind so I could provide my true experience and opinions on this fictional novel which is what this review is. I am not here to argue over any controversial aspects.<br /><br />This was a Traveling Friends read that had varying reactions in our discussion group. <br /><br />Thank you to my lovely local library for the loan of this incredible novel!</span>
  <a data-text-id="1677472311345224953" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2893140292" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer426846463947108056"> !! NOW AVAILABLE !!<br/><br/>4.5 Stars<br/><br/>Beginning at the end, or perhaps more accurately – after the end of the story, for a change. In the Author’s Note at the end of the story, Cummins writes: <br/><br/><i>”As I traveled and researched, even the notion of the American dream began to feel proprietary. There’s a wonderful piece of graffiti on the border wall in Tijuana that became, for me, the engine of this whole endeavor. I photographed it and made it my computer wallpaper. Anytime I faltered or felt discouraged, I c</i></span>
  <span id="freeText426846463947108056" style="display:none"> !! NOW AVAILABLE !!<br /><br />4.5 Stars<br /><br />Beginning at the end, or perhaps more accurately – after the end of the story, for a change. In the Author’s Note at the end of the story, Cummins writes: <br /><br /><i>”As I traveled and researched, even the notion of the American dream began to feel proprietary. There’s a wonderful piece of graffiti on the border wall in Tijuana that became, for me, the engine of this whole endeavor. I photographed it and made it my computer wallpaper. Anytime I faltered or felt discouraged, I clicked back to my desktop and looked at it: ‘También de este lado hay sueños.’ <br />	<b>“On this side, too, there are dreams.”</b></i> <br /><br />While there is much about this that seems painfully current, a story I would not be shocked to hear about through some <i>Breaking News</i> report which seem to occur much more often lately, it would be easy to forget the news is most often comprised of facts and figures and – especially lately – to be slanted to one side, politically, or the other. But this story is filled with a truth that needs, deserved to be shared, one that fuels the heart and soul of this book. It is a story about people enduring the worst, people who are so desperate for a life that doesn’t involve having to worry every day, every minute about the next minute, that they leave their home, friends and family for a dream. A dream that may, in reality, become their worst nightmare.<br /><br />The opening chapter grabbed me and pulled me in, an event occurs as this begins that prompts a mother and her young son to leave their home in Acapulco to escape the men who killed the other members of their family. Desperately anxious to make their way to a place of safety they need to head to the United States, but there are few people that she feels that she can turn to for help. They’re on their own. <br /><br />There’s an edge to this story that kept me reading, I cared about these people and wanted to see their dream come true, a dream for a life free of the sort of dangers that they’d fled. I wanted to see them reach a place of peace, and to see the possibility that their dreams might come true. <br /><br />A very timely read that moved me, shook me to the core, this is filled with heartache, as well as humanity, the kindness of strangers. While there is a struggle for their survival, and heartache, it is the fierce determination of a mother determined to give her child the best life she can, along with some exceptional, inspired writing, that moves this story along at an almost unputdownable pace. <br /><br />This is already in the works for a film, which will be brought to you by Imperative Entertainment, and yet, this book hasn’t even been published, yet. Do yourself a favour and read it first. <br /><br /><br /><br />Pub Date: 21 Jan 2020<br /><br /><br />Many thanks for the ARC provided by Flatiron Books through the Goodreads Giveaway program!</span>
  <a data-text-id="426846463947108056" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3032849241" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3032849241" />
    <a title="Jen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27709782-jen"><img alt="Jen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592393550p2/27709782.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3032849241?book_show_action=true">Mar 01, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jen" href="/user/show/27709782-jen">Jen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27709782-jen?shelf=5-star-favourites">5-star-favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27709782-jen?shelf=mexico">mexico</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3032849241" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7391309928250678105">American dirt is no American Pie. It is a compelling story that evoked emotions of fear and terror but also an appreciation of what a migrant must brave to triumph over crippling circumstances that lead them to take the journeys they do, to find a better place to live: For themselves and their families.<br/><br/>This is story of Lydia and son, Luca, who have survived a tragic slaughter of their family and only happened to survive by chance.<br/>A journey to escape the cartel and Mexico in hoping of reaching el</span>
  <span id="freeText7391309928250678105" style="display:none">American dirt is no American Pie. It is a compelling story that evoked emotions of fear and terror but also an appreciation of what a migrant must brave to triumph over crippling circumstances that lead them to take the journeys they do, to find a better place to live: For themselves and their families.<br /><br />This is story of Lydia and son, Luca, who have survived a tragic slaughter of their family and only happened to survive by chance.<br />A journey to escape the cartel and Mexico in hoping of reaching el Norte - the United States. This is also about the people they meet along the way with their own hardships and reasons for leaving their homes and families behind.<br /><br />This story gave me anxiety. I know there has been controversy over this one, which I’ve honestly steered clear of. In the author’s notes, Cummins states this is a work of fiction. However, the reality is, migrants often go through horrific conditions before they get to a safe haven. We can no longer think of them as a grey mass coming over a border; but rather that every migrant is a person with their own stories to be heard.<br /><br />This was a remarkable and memorable 5⭐️ read for me. Don’t let the controversy prevent you from picking this one up. Sometimes a cigar is just a cigar.<br />Kudos Cummins -You may not be the right ethnicity or colour to have written this, but this is true of so many writers. Good on you! ***And the movie rights have just been picked up***</span>
  <a data-text-id="7391309928250678105" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3124482423" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3124482423" />
    <a title="Dem" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2752994-dem"><img alt="Dem" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1552868566p2/2752994.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3124482423?book_show_action=true">Feb 05, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dem" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dem" href="/user/show/2752994-dem">Dem</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2752994-dem?shelf=thriller-crime">thriller-crime</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2752994-dem?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2752994-dem?shelf=recommended">recommended</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3124482423" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10590997170034365131"><b> A fast paced and heart stopping read, once I started I just galloped to the end as this was unputdownable </b><br/><br/>I have to say I felt like I was on the run with Lydia and Luca as my heart was pounding from the first page of this novel and I was sucked into the story. I loved the characters of Lydia and Luca and was rooting for them as the story progressed. There are plenty of twists and turns to keep the reader interested and I found myself staying up into the early hours of the morning to finish this</span>
  <span id="freeText10590997170034365131" style="display:none"><b> A fast paced and heart stopping read, once I started I just galloped to the end as this was unputdownable </b><br><br>I have to say I felt like I was on the run with Lydia and Luca as my heart was pounding from the first page of this novel and I was sucked into the story. I loved the characters of Lydia and Luca and was rooting for them as the story progressed. There are plenty of twists and turns to keep the reader interested and I found myself staying up into the early hours of the morning to finish this one. It’s not by any means a literary thriller but it certainly was a grippingly original novel for me. <br><br><i>A terrific fiction story about a mother named Lydia and her eight year old son Luca who are the only survivors of a targeted massacre by a Mexican Cartel that have been terrorising and taking over their home town of Acapulco, when 16 of their family members (including Lydia’s Journalist husband) have been murdered at a family event Lydia and her son have no choice but to go on the run and try and make their escape to the United States. </i> <br> <br>I wasn’t aware of the controversy surrounding this one until I had finished and read some of my friends reviews. I tend to stay away from reading reviews of new books I have purchased until after I have read my own copy. This way I don't end up with a tonne of books that never get read just because I have preconceived ideas. I also don’t buy into critic reviews again for the same reason. Thankfully we all react differently to books and I think that is what will make a book like American Dirt a great book club discussion book. This one reminded me a little of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/350540.The_Road" title="The Road by Cormac McCarthy" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1557160333l/350540._SY75_.jpg" alt="The Road by Cormac McCarthy" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> not in writing style but the atmosphere of the story. <br><br>Defiantly one I will remember a year from now and another copy for my real life book shelf.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10590997170034365131" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('qnWOK3rHibS191042Bp2SCt5vuLnpC0fipH1sspEmKigF/AS3Om6y6jsACSHpPnx3tSENydKbECWjzHsbg9brw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('mivgZ1ylzbOhD+vWf5UHWL9r3hy7cpRBNIuRu91/8feQSZ5e+ov+zLwUtsogK4jhSsbkyXuc1R4olVXleTQy8A==')})
  }

This is the story of how they did, and didn\'t; the unforeseen obstacles that propelled them into years of disillusionment and heartbreak; and the strength of a family determined to stay together.\n\nHere We Are: American Dreams, American Nightmares follows the lives of Aarti, the precocious scholarship kid at one of Manhattan\'s most elite prep schools, and her dad, the shopkeeper who mistakenly sells watches and calculators to the notorious Cali drug cartel.
